# NetOps (DevOps for Network Engineers): Automating Networks

> DevOps—a set of principles and practices combining software development and IT 
operations—is becoming the standard in corporate IT around the world. It enables a shorter delivery cycle, faster deployment, easier maintenance, and improving team culture. In this course, Eric Chou shows how to apply DevOps practices in a network engineering context, using easy to understand, hands-on examples. He co

>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=7)** While we will cover the fundamentals of DevOps, this course drills down on the application of these concepts in the network engineering environment.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=17)** To get the most out of this course, you might want to watch DevOps Foundations available here in the library, then come back to this course.

> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=25)** You should also be familiar with the basics of network management and engineering.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=29)** Don't worry, you do not need to be an expert in routing protocols or spanning tree, but you should be comfortable in basic configuration steps for network devices using Cisco iOS or other network operating systems.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=43)** We will operate in a Linux environment using the Bash Shell.

>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=69)** While the source files are available to you, this course is not meant to be a lab course where you follow along and perform the exact steps you see on screen to learn a certain technology.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=79)** Instead, we will be focused on the concepts and illustrate them using a variety of technologies.

> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=96)** The goal is to introduce to you the application of DevOps in network engineering using some of the tools you might already have so you could apply them in your own environment.

>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/what-you-should-know?u=76281980&t=117)** Let's get started.

### 1. DevOps for Network Engineers Overview

#### DevOps principles
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this session, let us explore the principles behind DevOps.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=4)** First of all, what is DevOps?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=6)** As one could guess from the terms, it is a combination of software development, dev, and IT operations, ops.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=13)** Traditionally, we would have separate semi-isolated teams, with one team handling the development of software features.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=20)** Once that is done, hand it over to the operations team for deployment and operation.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=25)** Over time, the two teams grow apart, because if they have different priorities, use different tools, and therefore, created some frictions between them.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=34)** For the majority of my career, I belonged squarely in the operations camp.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=38)** As an network engineer, I could recount many war stories of trying to provision VLANs at the last minute, scrambling to configure firewall rules, and making various last minute changes to the network in the operations and deployment phase, all the while, trying to make sure all the changes conform to the security standards.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=56)** On the other hand, DevOps is meant to bring the two teams together by leveraging the same technologies, share the same vocabularies, build better collaboration, and deliver faster results.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=68)** In this course, we will speak from the point of view of network operators, learning about the DevOps principles, tools, terminologies, and operations.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=78)** Another way to think about DevOps is with the three interrelated categories of people, process, and tools.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=85)** Everything we will talk about in this course falls into one of these three categories.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=89)** For example, in DevOps, we have a group of engineers who share the same principles, collaboratively define a set of processes conforming to these principles, and use a set of tools that enforce this process.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=102)** In turn, the tools will provide feedback to the engineers to further validate or tweak the principles and practices.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=110)** Keep these three interlocking components in mind as we move through the course.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=115)** As we have mentioned, the primary goal of DevOps is to shorten the software cycle from development to deployment.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=122)** In network engineering, we can also draw many parallels to the same design, develop, deploy, and feedback loop, as software development.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=132)** For example, we could put together a new data center design, develop an action plan to validate the design, then move forward with the deployment and monitoring.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=141)** A DevOps principle, such as version control, could be applied to all these three steps.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=146)** We could also benefit from another DevOps principles of making small incremental changes that could quickly respond to the changing environment.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=154)** The DevOps principles are highly related to the Agile and Lean software development, so let's take a look at the Lean principles and Agile development process before we move on to the DevOps principles.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=167)** What are some of the Lean principles?
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=169)** The number one principle is to eliminate waste.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=172)** What are waste?
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=174)** Waste are defined in everything not adding value to the customer.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=177)** Here are some of the waste defined in Lean, partially done work, extra features, relearning, task switching, waiting, handoffs, defects, and my personal favorite, management activities.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=190)** Lean thinks that the software development process is a continuous learning process based on iterations.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=195)** We're trying to solve problems for writing code, test with customer, learn the feedback, and rewrite the code if needed.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=203)** So the second principle is to speed up and amplify the learning process.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=207)** The third principle is to decide as late as possible.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=211)** Think about how much uncertainties there are in today's fast changing environment, such as new customer requirements might pop up, new competitors might enter the market, not to mention technology changes really, really fast, so by delaying big decisions as late as possible, we have some flexibilities built in.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=229)** The fourth principle is to deliver as fast as possible.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=233)** We all know technology changes rapidly.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=235)** The sooner we could get our products into the customer's hands, the faster we could receive the crucial feedback that we need to make the product better.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=244)** Other principles of Lean include empower the team for decision making, build integrity in the process, and optimize as whole.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=252)** Let's dive into [[Agile Software Development]] principles.
>
> **[4:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=257)** In customer focus, the highest priority is always customer satisfaction, and we should also embrace changes and adapt accordingly.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=267)** Always welcome the changing requirements.
>
> **[4:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=270)** We should aim to frequently deliver working software.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=273)** In a cross-functional team sense, collaboration means close daily co-operations between operators and developers.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=282)** We should aim for motivated teams, because projects that build around motivated people who should be trusted.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=289)** Also, face-to-face conversation is the best form of communication.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=294)** In Agile, continuous improvement means the team regularly reflects on how to be more effective.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=302)** Again, DevOps originated in software development, however, all of the principles we have seen in Lean and Agile are still applicable in network engineering.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=312)** Besides taking part as the operations team in an organization, let's look at how we could draw a parallel and adapt the DevOps principles within network engineering itself.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=323)** If we think about the network life cycle, initially, we'll receive some requirements from network.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=329)** It could be a corporate campus, a data center, or retail store, that we would design the network accordingly.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=335)** We would then develop the typology, necessary equipment, software licensing, port counts, and so on.
>
> **[5:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=343)** Then we would deploy the equipment per our design.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=346)** This could be the actual rack and stack, configuring the equipment, and all the necessary supporting infrastructure, such as IP management, DNS, DHCP, firewall policies, and so on.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=357)** Once it is deployed, we will continue to operate and monitor the network.
>
> **[6:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=362)** Maybe we are adding new users, VLANs, servers, security policies, and we will continue to monitor the health of the network to make sure they are operating in an optimal state.
>
> **[6:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=373)** Inevitably, even the best designed and operated network will need to be updated with new features, new business requirements, and we will repeat the cycles again.
>
> **[6:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=384)** Since the network engineering cycle is very similar to software development, in my opinion, the existing DevOps best practices can and should be adopted into network engineering as well.
>
> **[6:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=396)** In summary, the DevOps principles are having a collaboratively environment with joint responsibilities between development and operations teams.
>
> **[6:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=406)** Have a continuous development cycle.
>
> **[6:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=409)** Always try to speed our time to market with small teams.
>
> **[6:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=414)** And this is a big one, try to automate as many steps as possible.
>
> **[6:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-principles?u=76281980&t=419)** We should embrace failure and learn from them, and always, always be customer focused.

#### DevOps practices
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Having learned the DevOps principles, what are some of the DevOps practices?
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=6)** The first DevOps practice is to have a source of truth for the software code, documentation, device configuration or network state.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=15)** This usually means a distributed version control system that all team members could refer to.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=22)** The second DevOps practice is to have automated testing.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=26)** Because we're trying to put our emphasis on small incremental changes, we should aim to have automated testing that ensures we do not accidentally break things when these changes are made.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=38)** We should aim to have a system of continuous integration.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=42)** This means having a system for each developer and operations personnel put their changes into the source control, or the source of truth, as quickly as possible.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=53)** This change could range from software code, device state, network configuration, and so on.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=59)** It should also be pointed out the continuous integration means to have the changes make their way to the source of truth or version control system and does not equate to deployment.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=71)** Once we have continuous integration, we could take the next step for continuous delivery or continuous deployment.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=78)** What is the difference between the two?
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=80)** Sometimes we do not have control over deployment and just delivery, such as when we have changes in a updated doc or image or when we have a mobile app that is only deployed when the client pulls the changes in.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=95)** Another DevOps practice is to implement a high trust culture for individuals and between teams.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=101)** Examples of this practice could be peer review for changes as well as a blameless culture between developers and operators.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=110)** As mentioned, continuous integration and deployment is a practice where developers integrate the change into a version control repository.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=118)** Each integration could be verified by an automated testing process that could catch errors.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=125)** Optionally, the change could be deployed either automatically or with a manual push.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=130)** The system is crucial to the DevOps practice.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=133)** In this course, we will use a open source project called GitLab with built-in version control, issue tracking, code review, continuous integration, continuous delivery, and much more.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=146)** One of the newer job roles as a result of the DevOps movement is the rise of site reliability engineering, or SRE.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=156)** In the words of Google, SRE is what you get when you treat operations as if it is a software problem.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=164)** The goal of SRE is to protect, provide for, and monitor the software and system behind services.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=171)** One of the main concepts of SRE is the idea of the error budgets.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=177)** It is the uptime of the service as perceived by the user measured in time.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=182)** As Google is the company that started the SRE movement, feel free to follow the link to find out more about the SRE practices via the link provided.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=192)** As network engineers continue to adapt DevOps practice, sometimes you will hear the people refer to the job function and role as network DevOps.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=202)** Please feel free to check out the SRE description from Google or Network Computing's article about the coming together of DevOps into network engineering.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/devops-practices?u=76281980&t=211)** There are lots of practical examples of applying DevOps in the real world.

#### Unique network engineering challenges in DevOps
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this section, let's talk about some of the challenges we face in network engineering when we try to adapt DevOps mindsets and practices.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=8)** The goal is not to create shame or blame.

> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=15)** More importantly, what tools and process we can use to solve these challenges.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=21)** Traditionally, when we're planning and designing a network, we'll use tools such as Visio to diagram our network, perhaps use spreadsheet to keep track of IP address assignments, then use some kind of text file to keep track our standard configuration files.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=36)** These steps have worked for many years.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=38)** However, there's several problems with them.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=41)** The first problem is they require manual updates when changes occur.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=46)** The network diagram, for example, is almost out of date as soon as the first change occurs.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=51)** The spreadsheet and configuration templates also requires some engineers time and effort to maintain.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=57)** The second problem is once the change is made, there's not a lot of ways to keep track of the reasons behind the change or who made them.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=65)** In other words, we don't have accountability.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=69)** For example, why do we assign VLAN numbers the way we did?
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=72)** Nobody knows after a while.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=74)** It just has always been the way we did things.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=78)** Also a third problem is that these files are difficult to maintain across different teams.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=83)** Not everybody has as Visio, and not everybody uses the same way to keep track of different versions.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=88)** Many times we rely on emails and arbitrary naming conventions to know the latest version of these files.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=95)** The solution to these problems is to adapt a version control system, such as Git.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=101)** We could use the system to keep track of the modification histories, know who made the changes and when, all the while keeping them in a storage system that is distributed and redundant.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=111)** If you think the version control system is too good to be true, it is not.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=115)** It has been used and perfected over the years by software developers.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=119)** We're simply borrowing them for the operations team.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=123)** Another practice we have used for many years in network engineering is we use the production network as our source of truth.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=130)** What do we mean by a source of truth?
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=132)** According to Wikipedia, the single source of truth is the practice of structuring information models and associated files such as they're mastered and edited in only one place.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=143)** In network engineering, oftentimes, once the network is deployed, we will continue to make the necessary changes on the same production network.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=152)** For example, when we need to add more access control list entries or new VLANs, we just go directly to the network device and make that change.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=159)** This makes network changes risky.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=161)** Sometimes, a normal routine change could result in a big outage.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=166)** The management might lose confidence in network changes and further delay more changes or require a change control system that could potentially be prohibitive.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=176)** The solution to this problem is to keep a separate system outside of production for network configuration, related information and network state.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=185)** We could use database, version control system or dedicated servers for this purpose.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=191)** A nice open source project that have grown in popularity is a NetBox project as this single source of truth.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=199)** Another problem that we're all painfully aware is the fact that in traditional networking, the network equipment requires manual command line interface or CLI to make configuration changes.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=211)** CLIs are okay for initial configuration and learning, but not for repeated and redundant tasks.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=218)** This human-driven approach will result in more mistakes and create greater skill gaps.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=225)** Not to mention, they're sometimes very tedious to do.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=228)** Luckily, thanks to the community effort, we have a number of network automation frameworks and languages to choose from to eliminate this manual intervention.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=239)** We could use Python programing language and libraries, such as Nornir, Scrapli and NAPALM, to automate the manual configuration process.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=247)** We could also use automation frameworks, such as Ansible, to automate the changes without manual configuration.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=255)** Testing is a crucial component in DevOps.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=258)** But traditionally, we don't have a lot of testing.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=261)** One of the main reasons has to do with network testing environments.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=265)** The network equipments are specialized hardware devices, optimized to transport packets and frames over the wire as soon as possible.
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=274)** They're typically expensive.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=276)** And not a lot of organizations could afford a network testing environment.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=281)** I remember in previous jobs, as the makeshift testbed, we used to open brand new equipments, cable them up, station network to make sure everything works just fine, repackage them and ship them to the other sites for deployment.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=294)** This obviously make automated testing very difficult and is really not good for the DevOps testing principles.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=302)** Luckily, in recent years, we have seen more and more network vendors adopt virtualization of their hardware.
>
> **[5:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=310)** As we will do in this course, we could use a virtualized version of the network to conduct our testing.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=317)** Besides lack of testing equipment, traditionally, there were no widely available testing framework.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=322)** We have some commercial software that could perform SNMP, pings and trace routes, but that's about it.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=329)** In recent years, we have seen several promising testing framework that came to light.
>
> **[5:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=334)** Pytest is a Python testing framework that is widely used to test Python code.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=340)** PyATS is a testing framework that was originally developed at Cisco and was later released to be used by the community at no cost.
>
> **[5:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=348)** Batfish is the open source network configuration analysis tool that could be used in pre-change validation.
>
> **[5:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=355)** Suzieq is the open source multi-vendor network observability platform that could be used for network post-change validation.
>
> **[6:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=364)** The last issue I want to address is this mindset of you break it, you fix it.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=369)** Because we only have the production network as a source of truth as we have explained before, many times problems that tend to go dead could be concealed and obscured.
>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=379)** For example, when we added a new server and updated echo in a new deployment, the older sites were often not updated.
>
> **[6:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=387)** Or if we update the standard version of software on the newer network, in the newer network OS, many of the older devices were not updated due to oversight or risk.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=397)** The problem is if there're attempts to fix these legacy issues that results in outage, we have this you break it, you fix it mindset.
>
> **[6:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=406)** This discourages engineer's effort to fix the problem that are not obvious.
>
> **[6:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=411)** And they kind of just push them into the future until they could no longer be ignored.
>
> **[6:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=416)** The solution here, in my opinion, is the DevOps practice of making small incremental changes as well as adapt to blameless culture that will encourage cross-team collaboration.
>
> **[7:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=429)** I hope by now, you're convinced as I am that as network engineers, we have the tools and processes today to adopt DevOps culture and best practices.
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/unique-network-engineering-challenges-in-devops?u=76281980&t=439)** We could use these tools to help us become more productive and build a better culture.

> **Env Vars:** vlan (1), cli (1), napalm (1), snmp (1)
> **Tools:** command line (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Setting up a network DevOps lab
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/setting-up-a-network-devops-lab?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/setting-up-a-network-devops-lab?u=76281980&t=5)** In particular, we'll talk about how the lab is put together for this course.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/setting-up-a-network-devops-lab?u=76281980&t=10)** In our setup, we'll have a total two virtual machines.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/setting-up-a-network-devops-lab?u=76281980&t=14)** The first virtual machine or host will contain our virtualized network gears.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/setting-up-a-network-devops-lab?u=76281980&t=18)** And the second host will contain our GitLab Servers as well as our GitLab Runners.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/setting-up-a-network-devops-lab?u=76281980&t=24)** We'll go over the GitLab Server and GitLab Runners set up in more detail in just a bit, but just then as the overview the GitLab servers will have our code repository, our automation instructions, and those instructions get passed down to the GitLab Runners and the GitLab Runners are the actual processes that will execute those instructions, in this case to our network gears.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/setting-up-a-network-devops-lab?u=76281980&t=48)** For the network lab we'll utilize the latest Cisco modeling lab or CML.

#### Introduction to Git

> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=6)** If you recall from the last section, three of the most important DevOps principles are collaboration environments with joint responsibilities, continuous development, integration, and deployment cycle and automation in all three steps.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=21)** If we dig deeper into the three requirements, we could see the need for a joint space to collaborate is required for all three.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=28)** We need an environment to store all the latest progress.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=31)** This environment is where we will separate our progress into development, integration, and deployment and they all should be in automated formats.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=39)** In other words, we need a source control system.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=42)** A source control system, also known as revision or version control, is a way to manage code and related files to track changes and allow users to retrieve any of the previous versions of the original files.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=59)** Git is one of the most if not the most popular version control system in use today.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=64)** Some other VCSs you may have heard of are VCS, CVS, SVN and Mercurial, but Git is the most popular today and widely used for both public and private projects.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=76)** In fact, the source code for both the Linux kernel and Python are both using Git as their version control system.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=84)** Git was created by Linus Torvalds for the development of the Linux kernel back in 2005.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=91)** Git has a following focus right from the beginning.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=94)** It supports parallel, independent and simultaneous development of code repositories offline and online.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=101)** This allows thousands of engineers to work on the same repository at same time without needing to connect to a centralized server.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=108)** It is also fast and efficient with features such as compression and delta check.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=114)** Other advantages of Git include maintaining accountability by enforcing a changelog every time a change is made.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=122)** The data object in Git cannot be modified once they're created and placed in the database, making them immutable.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=130)** The integrity of the repository's insured as the different but related changes are performed together or not at all.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=139)** Each repository has complete history tracking of all revisions.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=144)** Also, Git has a very liberal usage license.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=147)** If we look back at the DevOps principles, Git is a perfect source control system that matches for what we are trying to achieve in DevOps.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=156)** If we think about version control systems, what we aim to do is to logically organize our files, manage changes, and identify who made the changes.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=167)** They help us keep track of issues and help us safely consolidate changes and revert them back if needed be.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=174)** Git trays the files in a tree format where the main branch is the trunk and everything else, such as features and bug fixes, are worked on independently as branches.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=184)** Once they're done, they're merged back into the main branch.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=188)** As an example, we see the main branch was created as having gone through changes A, B and C.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=195)** At point D, we created a new feature branch and worked on it as D and E.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=200)** At point E, we decided the feature is done and could be merged or pulled back into the main branch.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=208)** You may have heard the term GitOps.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=210)** It is a way to formalize these Git-related strategies such as pull-based or push-based deployments.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=219)** The basic steps of using Git include making your directory as a Git repository.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=225)** Git will start to keep track of the files.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=228)** We could then make changes to the files such as adding, deleting, or updating them.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=232)** These changes include making a new branch if needed be.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=237)** We will put the files into a staging area.

>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=246)** Finally, we can make the changes permanent by committing the changes.
>
> **[4:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/introduction-to-git?u=76281980&t=250)** If we have other repositories that we would like to synchronize of the local changes, we can optionally push the changes to them.

#### GitLab fundamentals
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In this section and the next few sections, we'll take a look at how GitLab fits into the DevOps picture.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=6)** We'll use GitLab as a tool to illustrate these practices and features that we can actually implement into our development environment today, and how they can help us enforce the DevOps principles and practices.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=19)** Let's start with the GitLab fundamentals.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=23)** GitLab describes itself as the DevOps platform that empowers organization to maximize the overall return on software development by delivering software faster and more efficient while strengthening security and compliance.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=39)** To me, the biggest difference between GitLab and other platforms is its integration of a source control system, as well as a CI/CD engine into the same platform.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=51)** On a daily basis, we're all by now familiar with the DevOps principles and practices.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=57)** But on a daily basis, as engineers, what we interact with closely is, one, the source control system, and two, is these automation processes, the stages that we could define to automate our task for us.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=71)** And it's nice to have those two pieces fit in together, as well as some of the other features that we'll see later on in this course that GitLab implement that fits pretty well with the DevOps principles that we've been learning and practicing so far.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=87)** Personally, I used to use GitHub, and I still do for some of my projects for repositories to store files.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=93)** Then, use another platform such as Jenkins, when I need to execute and run my automated delivery pipeline.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=99)** And because they were two separate tools, there were extra steps needed in order for the tools to work together, whereas in GitLab it's integrated into a single platform.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=110)** It is just a one-step shop integrating both, and the experience is a little bit more smoother, and that is why I choose to use GitLab as the underlying technology for this course.

>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=47)** If we use a compile language such as Java that requires taking the source code and compile it into a binary software before we could use it, this step is generally done in the build stage.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=62)** But as network engineers, we generally use non-compiled languages such as Java or Ansible.

> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=70)** So generally I would just interpret the build stage as just running the code and taking care of any steps needed before we run this code, such as PIP install certain libraries.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=81)** Since DevOps is all about streamline processes and automate our steps, testing is crucial in ensuring any new features or bug fixes do not break existing base nor does it introduce new issues.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=96)** And testing could be divided into certain categories such as unit tests, acceptance tests, integration testing and so on.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=104)** And testing used to be the job of QA engineers.

> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=108)** If you remember those roles, but it is better if we integrate them into the whole CI/CD process of course.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=115)** So testing is so important that we will actually dedicate many lessons later on in this course to discuss them in more detail and give more examples.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=127)** A staging environment is a near replica of the production environment.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=133)** They should replicate production as closely as possible.

>

> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=151)** As we have discussed before network engineering used to lack a staging environment due to cost and complexity, but with the advance of virtualization of network gears, we could actually pretty accurately replicate our production environment network, in the virtualized staging environment nowadays.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=170)** The deployment to production is generally the last step in our pipeline.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=174)** Of course, we'll continue to monitor and test the network, but deployed to is generally the last step that we really need to look out for.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=183)** And there are many deployment strategies.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=186)** It is not possible in all cases, but if we could we should make the deployment in stages.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=192)** For example, we could deploy the new changes into a small percentage of our devices, then gradually migrate to the rest of the devices.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=201)** In this way we could discover any possible defects and roll back if needed.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=206)** And if indeed, unfortunately we introduce some new bugs or break some stuff, the blast radius could actually be smaller that way.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=216)** Another note for deployed to production in my experience, most organization will automate all the steps up to staging but leave deployment to production as a manual step.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-devops-ci-cd-pipelines?u=76281980&t=229)** Generally this step in between staging and deployment to production would have some more reviews, possible management approvals, or we leave the change into a specific maintenance window, depending on the potential impacts.

#### GitLab pipeline example: Deploy
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] So far our steps has been executed sequentially and automatically.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=5)** What if we want, as we've mentioned before, a lot of times we want our final deployment to be manually pushed.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=13)** So we'll run our co-quality check, we'll run some testing, and before we push it down to actual production deployment, we want to have that final step as a manual push.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=24)** Maybe we want to set a particular maintenance window, maybe we want more reviews, more eyes on the code, so on.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=31)** So how can we do that?
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=33)** It's actually quite simple.
>

> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=39)** And let's just say after we do the Flake8 check, we do the preparation and we want the last job to be pushed out manually.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=49)** So we have this keyword and say when that is manual, an additional keyword that's usually often used in concurrency is allow failure, which I'll set it to false.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=65)** What this does is typically, even when you have a manual push, if it fails, it's not going to stop the other jobs from executing after it, but what I want is if it fails, then I don't want any job to execute behind it.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/gitlab-pipeline-example-deploy?u=76281980&t=80)** So I would just say allow failure equals to false.

### 4. Testing in DevOps

#### Testing fundamentals

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's talk about testing fundamentals in DevOps.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=4)** DevOps allows development and operation teams to collaborate smoothly and deliver results continuously.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=11)** We have seen relevant tools and technologies that could help us do that in this course.

> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=16)** One area we have lightly touched on, but haven't spent a lot of time going over is testing.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=22)** Testing is an integral part to ensure we have high quality software and operation procedures by detecting errors and conflicts as soon as possible.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=33)** Of course, testing is nothing new.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=35)** Any form of verification is a form of testing.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=39)** In traditional testing, we have had dedicated testing teams that perform quality assurance at the tail end of the development cycle.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=48)** Or we would have infrastructure testing and monitoring tools after we deploy our gears.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=54)** There are manual processes that might take days or weeks to complete.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=58)** Because of the manual process, it could be error prone and difficult to keep a standard of quality over time.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=65)** In DevOps, testing is a continuous and automated process.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=70)** They're integrated into every step of the way.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=73)** They're also not just a responsibility of one team, testing responsibilities are shared amongst all team members.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=81)** This shared responsibility should make a lot of sense.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=84)** I mean, who else can do a better job of testing than each of the subject matter experts.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=91)** Testing could also be categorized into several types.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=95)** In unit testing, we test a small unit of a function, code block or procedure.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=100)** This is the smallest testable part of a code or operation.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=105)** In functional testing, we try to ensure our code or operation is acting in accordance to our specified requirements.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=114)** For system testing, we want to verify and evaluate if multiple components are working well together while fully integrated.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=123)** For end to end testing, we test both the functionality as well as the performance of an application under production-like environment.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=132)** Other test includes performance, load, security, compliance or API testing.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=139)** As we can see from the list, the test moves from small to large in scale.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=144)** The end to end testing will require the most time and effort while unit tests will require the least.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=151)** In practice, we will spend most of the time in unit test because they're the easiest to do and can point us to a more precise cause of an error if any.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=162)** If you recall from previous lessons, network engineers used to have difficult times with testing environments because network hardware is expensive and difficult to manipulate.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=172)** With the advance of virtualization, we could typically use platforms such as CML, GNS3 and Eve-NG for many of the tests we want to do.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=182)** We also have several testing frameworks available to choose from.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/netops-devops-for-network-engineers-automating-networks/testing-fundamentals?u=76281980&t=186)** We can use pytest to test our Python code as well as frameworks such as pyATS, Batfish and Suzieq to simplify our narrow testing.
